1932.11.23

The Executive Council Will Reconvene This Afternoon, With Lytton Explaining the Report

The External Affairs Ministry Completes Drafting a Rejoinder to Japanese Counterarguments; Matsuoka Widely Visits Representatives of Major Powers to Alleviate Anti-Japanese Sentiment

(Nanjing) Government authorities received a telegram from Gu Weijun on the evening of the 22nd, reporting that there would be no meeting on the 22nd and that the agenda for the 23rd would include: 1) Lytton responding to the Japanese representative's arguments against the report; 2) representatives of various countries questioning the Japanese representative and inquiring whether the Japanese government has the sincerity to peacefully resolve the Sino-Japanese incident. The meeting would be suspended on the 24th and 25th and would reconvene on the 26th to submit the report and the minutes of this Executive Council meeting for approval and transfer them to the Committee of Nineteen and the League of Nations General Assembly. The rejoinder drafted by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to refute the Japanese counterarguments has been completed and is scheduled to be released on the 23rd. As for the specialized issues in the Japanese counterarguments, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs has instructed the three representatives stationed in Geneva to refute them point by point as appropriate. (Special dispatch from the 22nd)

(Nanjing) According to government officials, reports from various sources and foreign newspaper articles prove that countries around the world are fully aware of Japan's aggression against China. Recently, the release of the Japanese counterarguments has further revealed its frantic attitude of blaming third parties. It is clear that Japan intends to be hostile to peace and has no regard for other countries. Therefore, the atmosphere in Geneva is becoming increasingly unfavorable to Japan. China should seize this opportunity to strengthen internal unity as a backing for diplomacy and to connect with friendly countries to support justice. (Special dispatch from the 22nd)

▲ A Dentsu dispatch from Geneva on the 21st reports that in today's speech at the Council, Japanese representative Matsuoka resolutely refused to change Japan's position on the Manchurian issue. Chinese representative Gu Weijun said that he had received reports that if the Manchurian issue could not be resolved satisfactorily, the boycott of Japanese goods would likely expand. The two sides then clashed head-on, resulting in a major crisis and a state of deadlock.

▲ A Reuters dispatch from Geneva on the 22nd reports that the League of Nations feels that Matsuoka and Gu Weijun are both speaking from absolutely irreconcilable positions and are not seeking points of agreement based on the Lytton Report, which will make the work of the Executive Council very difficult. Therefore, the nature of the issue is very complex and cannot be resolved satisfactorily. The Council members are currently holding private talks to discuss the meeting tomorrow, but for the time being, everyone's attention has shifted to the issue of Germany and the Disarmament Conference. German Foreign Minister Neurath can only stay here for a few days and must leave by Saturday or Sunday.

▲ A Reuters dispatch from Geneva on the 21st reports that the discussions of the League of Nations Executive Council may not last long. The entire issue will be submitted to a special session of the League of Nations General Assembly as soon as possible, and the issue of reconvening the Committee of Nineteen will be decided by the General Assembly.

▲ A Dentsu dispatch from Geneva on the 21st reports that the next Council meeting is scheduled to be held at 3:30 p.m. on the 23rd. Council President Valleray and major powers such as Britain and France intend to communicate with members of the Commission of Inquiry and key figures of the countries concerned during this period to prevent empty discussions at the next Council meeting, hoping for substantive progress.

(Nanjing) The League of Nations Executive Council convened on the 21st, with representatives from China and Japan making political statements. On the 23rd, Sir Lytton will deliver a speech to explain the report in detail, followed by speeches from representatives of various countries. This marks the beginning of the League of Nations Executive Council's formal discussion of the Lytton Report. According to diplomatic observers, Lytton's speech on the 23rd will be the same in content as his broadcast speech on the 19th, but more extensive and detailed. Diplomatic circles believe that Lytton's statement that the Commission of Inquiry does not recognize the so-called "Manchukuo" and that Japan's recognition of "Manchukuo" is unreasonable is extremely fair and crucial. They also believe that the Executive Council will accept Lytton's fair opinion and formally declare that it does not recognize "Manchukuo" before the opening of the meeting. As for Lytton's statement on using conference methods to peacefully resolve disputes, they place endless hope on the League of Nations and hope that it will be realized quickly and satisfactorily. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 22nd)

▲ A Hualian News Agency dispatch from Tokyo on the 22nd reports that, according to Japanese sources, Matsuoka Yosuke visited French representative Poncet at 7 p.m. yesterday and earnestly requested French support for Japan with certain conditions. Today, he will visit representatives of Britain, Italy, and Germany to seek their assistance.

(Nanjing) The Japanese delegation reported its League of Nations strategy to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs from France yesterday: 1) Actively engage within the Executive Council to gain the understanding of the major powers and control the General Assembly; 2) declare its sincerity in upholding the League of Nations Covenant and the Kellogg-Briand Pact to appease the weaker nations and avoid agitation in the General Assembly; 3) elaborate on the favorable points in the Commission of Inquiry report and refute the unfavorable points, striving to avoid disagreements with the major powers and ensuring that the Empire reaps practical benefits; 4) avoid heated debates with the Chinese side in the meeting and outwardly offer cooperation; 5) promote the resolution of the Manchurian issue by transferring it to direct negotiations between China, Japan, and "Manchukuo" as a last resort. (Shenshi News Agency dispatch from the 22nd)

▲ A Reuters dispatch from London on the 22nd reports that there is much debate about whether the issue of the Three Eastern Provinces of China should be handled by the League of Nations Executive Council or the League of Nations General Assembly. There is a new proposal to convene a special meeting of the signatory countries of the 1921 Washington Treaty to handle the case. If so, the United States will also participate in the discussion. The Conservative Party's Daily Telegraph said in today's editorial that the Manchurian case is of great importance to the general problems of the world and strongly urged the government to decide on the fundamental principles on which to act if intervention is unfortunately necessary, otherwise Britain will be caught in a very dangerous dispute. Britain should not assist China's demands on the Manchurian issue, causing Japan to withdraw from the constraints of the League of Nations, as the future of the Disarmament Conference will collapse as a result, and the outcome of naval disarmament will be greatly unfavorable to Britain and the world.

The Composition of the Committee of Nineteen

(Nanjing) According to diplomatic sources, the fourteen countries attending this League of Nations Executive Council meeting are Germany, Britain, France, Italy, Spain, Poland, Mexico, Ireland, Guatemala, Panama, Norway, Czechoslovakia, China, and Japan. As for the composition of the Committee of Nineteen, in addition to China and Japan, the fourteen countries mentioned above also include Switzerland, Colombia, Hungary, Sweden, Belgium, Yugoslavia, and the Netherlands. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 22nd)

Puppet Representatives Wander in Paris

▲ A Hualian News Agency dispatch from Tokyo on the 22nd reports that Ding Shiyuan, a puppet from the false organization, was refused entry by the Swiss government on his way from Paris to Geneva. He is currently wandering in the suburbs of Paris, in a dilemma. He has telegraphed the Kwantung Army and the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs in Tokyo for assistance. Because the puppet cannot enter Geneva, the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs is extremely anxious.

The United States Maintains Strict Silence

▲ A Havas dispatch from Washington on the 22nd reports that since the beginning of the Geneva Conference, the State Department has been extremely silent on the issue of Manchuria, fearing that the outside world will misunderstand the attitude of the United States. However, well-informed sources believe that if the League of Nations maintains a favorable attitude toward China, all the powers will declare that they refuse to recognize "Manchukuo." It is said that the United States has long held this intention.

Dr. Gu Weijun Refutes Matsuoka's Fallacies

▲ A Reuters dispatch from Geneva on the 21st reports that this afternoon, Dr. Gu Weijun spoke on behalf of China at a special meeting of the League of Nations Executive Council. Gu originally intended to read from a prepared speech, but he did not fully follow it. Gu first responded to the remarks made by Japanese representative Matsuoka this morning, saying that if people believed Matsuoka's words, it would be tantamount to believing that Japan is a gentle lamb in China's embrace. Fortunately, the world has the Lytton Report to prove that this is not the case. He wants to reserve criticism of Matsuoka's points, but now he wants to say a few words.

▲ Discarding Sacred Treaties Even assuming that Matsuoka's words are not false, the question remains: to what extent is Japan's military aggression reasonable? If the world's interpretation of the Kellogg-Briand Pact is the same as Japan's, then what is the benefit of complying with such a treaty? He believes that it is more appropriate to interpret the nature and meaning of self-defense from the text of the Kellogg-Briand Pact itself. Gu said that he would read the Chinese government's opinion on the Lytton Report, first stating that as a Chinese staff member, he was subjected to unwarranted restrictions and prohibitions in the Three Eastern Provinces, so that he could not inspect the site of the incident, nor could he find a way to make Chinese witnesses appear before the Lytton Commission of Inquiry, while Japanese staff members enjoyed freedom everywhere in China. In comparison, the treatment was very different.

▲ Obstructing China's Unification One of the biggest difficulties China encounters in the process of construction is Japan's repeated actions to prevent its realization. Japan constantly accuses China of not being unified to the world, while continuing to implement its policy of preventing China's unification. Whether Japan wants China to be unified is a question. It is clear that the Japanese are concerned that China's unification will be detrimental to Japan's development policy.

▲ Threatening Peace in the Far East The Japanese continental policy is the crystallization of centuries of Japanese Bushido teachings, the purpose of which is to conquer Asia, with China as the first step. This continental policy is truly a great disaster for peace in the Far East. What is even more dangerous is that behind this policy there is an uncontrollable military party, which is one of the most powerful of all Japanese war machines and wants to implement its主張 with an iron fist.

▲ Boycotting is Passive Self-Defense The reason why the Chinese people continue the boycott movement is to oppose Japan's policy of aggression. This spontaneous mass movement cannot be completely separated from any government. This is a legitimate method of self-defense. The Chinese central government can only acquiesce to it. However, the Chinese government is closely monitoring it. This has been confirmed by the Lytton Report. Therefore, since the Japanese army began its aggression in the Three Eastern Provinces, there have been very few accidents. The Chinese government, under the current circumstances, is enacting legislation to boycott Japanese merchants and goods, and it cannot be said that it is unreasonable to formulate and implement a more consistent method of boycott. However, the fact that China has not yet taken this step is enough to show the characteristics of the Chinese government's policy of patience and moderation. The question of whether the implementation of an organized boycott is incompatible with friendly relations cannot arise until another prior question has been decided. What is this prior question? It is whether Sino-Japanese relations can still be considered friendly at a time when Japan is wantonly invading Chinese territory. China certainly wants to seek a peaceful solution through the League of Nations, but China feels that it is necessary to stop the invading army from advancing one after another whenever possible. China has chosen this form of passive resistance, which is more humane because it is bloodless. If armed resistance is used, bloodshed will inevitably occur. If it is said that China should not boycott, then it is directly剥削合法与和平的自卫工具矣.

▲ Unreasonable Actions of the Japanese Army The Lytton Report has proved that China's claim that the Shenyang Incident cannot be a reason for Japanese military action. Since the Shenyang Incident cannot be a reason for the Japanese army's actions there, there is even less reason for the Japanese army to simultaneously invade Chinese territory in Changchun, Jilin, and Yingkou that night. Looking at the Jinzhou Incident on October 10 last year, it is even more proof of the lack of integrity of the Japanese authorities. The Japanese have destroyed the administrative power of Jinzhou, Jilin, and many places in the Three Eastern Provinces, and still claim that there is no public order in the Three Eastern Provinces. Page 127 of the Lytton Report mentions that although the Japanese authorities have made solemn guarantees to the League of Nations, they are still carrying out their methods of coercion and assimilation. This statement is also worthy of attention.

▲ Resisting World Public Opinion Dr. Gu said after describing the Shanghai Incident in January of this year that there is still one thing that is shocking evidence of Japan's resistance to the world, which is Japan's formal recognition of "Manchukuo," completely disregarding the solemn responsibilities of the League of Nations Covenant and international treaties, as well as its repeated promises to the League of Nations Executive Council. If the Japanese do not want to take over China's sovereignty and replace it, then the actions of the Japanese army in South Manchuria will have no purpose. China is concerned about this, and the Japanese authorities have angrily refuted it. However, neutral news agencies, such as the Associated Press and Reuters, have reported that the Japanese are actively seizing the civil administration of the Three Eastern Provinces.

▲ Reserving Claims for Compensation Dr. Gu continued that the solution to this issue should be left to a special session of the League of Nations General Assembly. China has been guaranteed against foreign aggression, and now it cannot allow China to abandon its rights before the aggression as a result of this aggression. The Lytton Report approves of the Chinese government's attitude and believes that any discussion between China and other countries must be held under the League of Nations Covenant and the Kellogg-Briand Pact, based on China's rights. The Chinese government is prepared to use any suggestion that is consistent with this general principle as the basis for discussion. The Chinese government reserves the right to claim compensation for Japan's acts of aggression.

▲ Unfulfilled Obligation to Withdraw Troops Japan's obligation to withdraw troops under the repeated resolutions of the League of Nations last year still exists. The withdrawal of troops is still necessary and is a prerequisite for the fundamental resolution of the Sino-Japanese dispute. The pressure of military occupation and the pressure of faits accomplis obtained by force must be eliminated. This is a necessary move. If this necessity is not recognized, then the solution to this dispute cannot be properly discussed.

▲ Quickly Adopt Effective Measures The Lytton Report describes the true situation in the Three Eastern Provinces in detail and clearly. The time has come for the League of Nations to take swift and effective action, to uphold justice, and to maintain world peace. The only way to do this is to quickly and effectively resolve the Sino-Japanese conflict based on the principles of fairness and justice stipulated in international treaties. This is what China hopes for. Dr. Gu's speech devoted a portion to a historical account of Japan from the 16th century to the Tanaka Memorial, in order to prove Japan's unchanging ambitions towards China. The Executive Council adjourned at 6:05 p.m. The next meeting is scheduled for 3:30 p.m. on Wednesday.

▲ A Reuters dispatch from Geneva on the 21st reports that Matsuoka told guests today that Dr. Gu Weijun's陈述 had nothing new. He greatly admired the Chinese representative's polite speech, as if it came from an old friend. As for the Tanaka Memorial mentioned by Dr. Gu, he can point out the name of the forger when necessary. He believes that there is no need to refute the Chinese complaints, but he is only prepared to detail the situation in China.

Japan Threatens to Withdraw from the League of Nations, But People in the League of Nations Do Not Mind

▲ A Guomin News Agency dispatch from Geneva on the 22nd reports that many representatives in the League of Nations have always regarded Japan's threats to withdraw from the League of Nations as insignificant. Today, they have paid a little more attention than before, but few still believe that the Japanese are determined to implement it. Recently, newspapers have interpreted Japan's views on the Lytton Report and Matsuoka's speech at the League of Nations as indicating that the Japanese representative has been ordered to withdraw if the actions of the League of Nations are not satisfactory to the Japanese. Therefore, the representatives have also turned to pay attention to it, and at the same time informally discussed the issue of the islands in the South Pacific entrusted to Japan, and whether they can be a powerful factor to prevent Japan from withdrawing from the League of Nations. However, this has raised a serious question of whether Japan would be willing to have the League of Nations take back the entrusted rule and entrust it to another country after it has been entrusted with the rule. One observer said that these islands are the first naval defense line for Japan's attack on the East. Although they are scattered over 100,000 square miles of ocean, their position is enough to endanger the communication lines between the United States and the Philippines, and between the Panama Canal and the Philippines. Naval experts here all say that if there is a naval battle between Japan and the United States in the Pacific, Japan can use these islands as naval bases to block American warships, which will make it difficult for the American fleet to succeed without the help of the British fleet. Since these islands are so important to Japan, the Japanese will not easily give them up. If the League of Nations really intends to transfer them to another country, the United States will also compete for them. Another observer believes that if Japan withdraws from the League of Nations and refuses to give up the entrusted islands, it will inevitably convene a meeting of the signatory countries of the Four-Power Treaty of Britain, the United States, France, and Japan.

The British People's Rights Alliance Issues an Important Declaration

Even if Japan Withdraws from the League of Nations, It Will Still Be Bound by the Covenant

▲ A Guomin News Agency dispatch from London on the 21st reports that today, the People's Rights Alliance issued a declaration signed by Lansbury (leader of the Labour Party) and Wells, stating that the crisis in the Sino-Japanese dispute is developing and will have a decisive impact not only on the future of the Far East, but also on the issue of disarmament. It is worrying that Japan will decide to withdraw from the League of Nations after the League of Nations has a resolution that the Japanese deem unfavorable. However, one point must be clarified: even if Japan decides to withdraw from the League of Nations, it will still be bound by the Covenant unless it has fulfilled its international obligations under the League of Nations Covenant. Furthermore, if Britain expresses its willingness to cooperate with the United States to jointly maintain the Nine-Power Treaty, it may still be able to prevent Japan from withdrawing from the League of Nations. Finally, the People's Rights Alliance also suggested that if the League of Nations General Assembly declares Japan to be a treaty-breaking aggressor, then all countries should immediately ban the sale of all arms and ammunition to Japan.

A Glimpse of Opinions from Various Countries

▲ A Reuters dispatch from Paris on the 21st reports that only two newspapers today have editorials discussing the Eastern Provinces incident, and these two editorials can represent the views of the two extremes. The "Liberté," a right-wing newspaper that has always been pro-Japanese, said that Japan is maintaining order in an area of anarchy and is fulfilling an obligation to mankind. The "Le Peuple," a pro-Chinese socialist newspaper, said that the League of Nations should maintain its prestige and force Japan to return the Eastern Provinces to China. It is generally believed that the League of Nations has encountered a major crisis.

▲ A Reuters dispatch from Paris on the 22nd reports that French newspapers have little criticism of the arguments of the Chinese and Japanese representatives. The Paris Morning Post said in today's editorial that observing the reasons held by both sides, there is clearly no appropriate procedure for reconciliation and mediation. The League of Nations seems to be careful to decline and let others handle it. Moreover, the opinions of the League of Nations General Assembly are divergent, and it is especially necessary to follow this path. Le Petit Parisien questioned the qualifications of the League of Nations Executive Council, saying that the matter should be handled by the League of Nations General Assembly, because it is the General Assembly that can decide such issues.

▲ A Reuters dispatch from Berlin on the 22nd reports that only the Germania newspaper in Germany criticized the meeting in Geneva yesterday, saying that the League of Nations will not change its old ways on the Manchurian issue. It has made no decision in the past fourteen months and will still shelve it without a decision. The tragedy of the Manchurian conflict shows that the League of Nations is an inadequate and incomplete organization, and is not sufficient to carry out the important work proposed by Herriot in his construction plan. Britain and France have never had the enthusiasm for decisive action, and the repeated delays of the Manchurian issue are related to Britain and France. What Germany is most concerned about is avoiding a precedent, fearing that Germany will be in the same position in the future and will be adversely affected by this precedent. The newspaper concluded pessimistically that the hope of resolving the Far Eastern conflict in Geneva is equal to zero.

▲ A Reuters dispatch from Ottawa on the 21st reports that Canada will not criticize the debate in Geneva for the time being and will express its views after the League of Nations discusses the Sino-Japanese dispute. Prime Minister Bennett said in the House of Commons today that Canada's representative in Geneva will take an honest and selfless attitude toward Sino-Japanese relations. It is not appropriate for the government to make a hasty comment without studying the debate on land disputes in detail.

▲ A Reuters dispatch from Tokyo on the 22nd reports that all evening newspapers published the speeches of the Chinese and Japanese representatives at yesterday's League of Nations Executive Council meeting in a prominent position, but did not comment on them. Although the newspapers focus on the debate at the League of Nations in Geneva, they pay even more attention to the dispute between the Minister of Railways and the Minister of the Interior regarding the budget for civil engineering procedures. If the public cannot agree on a settlement, the cabinet may break down.

(Shenyang) Sixty-eight members of the Liaodong Righteous Army were arrested in Andong County and imprisoned in two separate locations. Current Commentary

Sino-Japanese Conflict Beyond Geneva Also -- Xuan

1. The Focal Point of the Sino-Japanese Conflict

The Executive Council of the League of Nations convened in Geneva on the 21st at 11:00 AM. The main agenda item was the discussion of the "Lytton Report." Thus, the diplomatic battle lines between China and Japan have been drawn. In terms of personnel, our representative, Mr. Gu Weijun, is a leading figure in the diplomatic world. The Japanese side's Matsuoka Yosuke is also a talented individual jointly recommended by their military and Ministry of Foreign Affairs. Although Japan vigorously promotes the argument that the League of Nations has an "insufficient understanding" of Eastern issues, it proceeds cautiously in international diplomacy. Their written rebuttal to the Lytton Report does everything possible to slander our country. On the other hand, they spare no effort in sophistry to justify their aggression and occupation, claiming that Japan's attack on the three northeastern provinces was for the sake of peace in the Orient, out of self-defense, to protect Japan's security, and to maintain the sanctity of treaties. However, examining the reality, international treaties such as the Nine-Power Treaty and the Kellogg-Briand Pact, which are jointly adhered to by the world, have been turned into waste paper by Japanese swords and guns. Although the original order in the three northeastern provinces was not ideal, the people could still manage to live there. Since being violently seized by the Japanese military, roads are almost impassable, and the fields are barren. What is this called tranquility? Where is the peace?

We have long stated that the League of Nations is powerless. Currently, various countries in the world are plagued by economic recession. Although countries like the United Kingdom, the United States, and France are nominally leaders, they are, in fact, outwardly strong but inwardly weak, lacking the real strength to restrain Japan's violence and monopoly. Therefore, we believe that seeking assistance from foreigners and seeking justice within the framework of the League of Nations will inevitably be fruitless.

Therefore, in addressing the China-Japan problem outside of Geneva diplomacy, China should adopt a practical national struggle that relies on its own strength, possessing a strong determination and establishing a long-term plan. Only then can we engage in a life-or-death battle with our current powerful enemy.

Let us further elaborate on this. The weakness of our military strength and the impoverishment of our people in addressing the Northeast issue are important factors in our failure. Moreover, our country has a vast territory, abundant natural resources, and a dense population, further characterized by future market expansion. Various countries are expanding their commercial influence in China. Are we willing to lag behind forever and become mere carriers of goods for others? Or will we rise up and become self-reliant? What various countries lack and suffer from most at present is commodity surplus and a narrow market. We have a vast market but cannot make good use of it, leading to exploitation by a powerful enemy. Japan is nominally a strong country, but economically, it has extremely limited natural resources such as minerals, forestry products, and agricultural products, and cannot be self-sufficient. Its specialty lies in the textile industry. Although our country is relatively backward, it is not difficult to engage in economic competition with Japan in a short period. Moreover, Japan is already feeling the narrowness of its market and has goods but nowhere to sell them. The only market is in our country. If we can rise up in time and engage in active economic competition with them, using our own domestic market to counter their crudely manufactured goods, we should have lasting resistance, no matter how weak our country may be.

2. National Mobilization

Before Japan seized our three northeastern provinces, it called on its citizens with the unified slogan: "National Crisis Imminent." It used the pretext of "Manchuria" being its national defense line and lifeline to inspire its citizens. Therefore, before the September 18th Incident occurred, the Second Division and the Twentieth Division had already secretly mobilized and moved to the South Manchuria Railway area to carry out the occupation of Liaoning and Jilin provinces. Although the military authorities in the area adopted a policy of non-resistance, patriotic youths refused to retreat, willingly fighting for the nation and sacrificing themselves. They rose up from the fields, wielding outdated weapons to confront the Japanese military. Although they did not deal a fatal blow to Japan or recover the lost territories, the Japanese warlords were clearly flustered. The slogan of national mobilization has spread throughout Japan. In addition to the original force of approximately 40,000 troops that created the September 18th Incident, the Eighth Division ("West"), the Tenth Division ("Hirose"), the Fourteenth Division ("Matsuki"), and other special units were added to "Manchuria," totaling no less than 100,000 troops. As a result, not only did they fail to pacify the Northeast, but they also made the order in that region increasingly chaotic. However, their ambition has not been slightly curbed, and they have also carried out economic mobilization, implementing a widespread dumping policy, suffocating the sales of Chinese-made products in the Chinese market. Only then can Japan's policy of monopoly be developed, and only then can there be a way out for imperialist aggression.

At this time, our country is in this difficult situation, subjected to their military oppression and economic encirclement. If we only seek to open up a new path through diplomatic negotiations, we fear that we will ultimately have no way to preserve ourselves. We can only improve our national front, on the one hand, and devote our full efforts to economic construction on the other. We must resolutely abandon the empty talk of the past and bury ourselves in work, rectify internal affairs, restore old industries, and develop new industries. Then, the current unemployed masses will gradually disappear, and the social unrest will naturally be cleared away. Do we not see the Soviet Union? Their current First and Second Five-Year Plans are fundamentally very similar to Mr. Sun Yat-sen's nation-building strategies. They were able to make rapid economic progress in four years. Although our country and Soviet ideology take different paths, their efforts in industrial construction are indeed valuable lessons for our country to learn from. Our citizens should strive for economic development and construction, and we must not delay any longer. The China-Japan problem must be based on the economic strength of the nation as a competitive foundation. As for the boycott movement, it seems to be an active action on the surface, but in essence, it is still passive work. It only stops at boycotting goods, which only makes the other side feel pain, while we ourselves have not established anything. Therefore, our national mobilization does not necessarily have to rely entirely on military victories or diplomatic negotiations. The final settlement will depend on the efforts of our citizens in economic construction.

Chongqing Troops Enter Luzhou City; Tang, Pan, and Wang Divisions Advance Westward

Rumored to Have Occupied Weiyuan, Rongxian, Jiang'an, Etc.; Liu Xiang States That He Will Not Cease Military Operations Until Xufu is Captured; Chongqing Telegram Claims That the 24th Army Has Retreated and is Stationed in Jiading

(Hankou) Liu Wenhui's troops abandoned Luzhou on the 19th and concentrated towards Xufu. Chongqing troops entered Luzhou City on the 21st. The city was nearly half destroyed by aerial bombing, with many refugees. Gentry and merchants are organizing disaster relief. Liu Xiang stated that he will not cease military operations until Xufu is captured. Therefore, the Tang, Pan, and Wang divisions continue to advance. It is rumored that the right wing has occupied Weiyuan and Rongxian, and the left wing has occupied Jiang'an, which is about a hundred miles away from the rear of the provincial army, according to a special dispatch on the 22nd.

(Hankou) Deng Xihou telegraphed on the 19th, stating that he resolutely requested a ceasefire from all parties in response to the demands of the people, with a firm intention. All the generals responded immediately with telegrams of support. It is heard that Liu Wenhui will be the first to agree and that he will also issue another telegram stating the process of continuous concessions, expressing his unwillingness to prolong or expand the war. He only seeks to preserve some vitality during the national crisis. He is willing to sacrifice everything. It is heard that he will further abandon Xufu and retreat to Jiading if necessary, and is even willing to make concessions to Tian. There are currently no conflicts between the two armies in Chengdu City, but they are still confronting each other outside the city, according to a special dispatch on the 22nd.

(Nanjing) A certain agency received a telegram from Chongqing on the 20th, stating that Pan's division of the 21st Army is attacking Xufu. Tang's division occupied Rongxian on the 20th, and Xu's brigade occupied Weiyuan, according to a special dispatch on the 22nd.

(Nanjing) News from the Sichuan Army Representative Office: (1) Liu Xiang's troops crossed Nanxi and advanced towards Xufu, only a river away from the provincial army. The air force followed them to Luzhou and flew to Xufu to threaten them. The strength of the 24th Army has been reduced by two-fourths and cannot hold out for long. (2) As a result of the street fighting in Chengdu, Liu and Tian's troops suffered a total of more than 600 deaths and more than 1,000 injuries each. Approximately 3,000 civilians died. More than 400 buildings in the main street were burned down. The losses in the city outskirts or alleys are not counted. All of the most valuable shops have been destroyed, with total losses exceeding ten million. The people are panicked and are leaving the province to avoid the chaos. Deng Xihou's announcement to dissuade them has been ineffective. (3) The allied generals are extremely angry at Liu Wenhui's use of divisive schemes and collusion with Tian's rebellious troops, and they advocate for their complete annihilation, according to a special dispatch on the 22nd.

(Nanjing) Liu Xiang telegraphed to Nanjing on the 20th, stating that the enemy troops in Luzhou City had sent deputies and foreign gentry to express their willingness to be reorganized. Xiang has agreed to accept their surrender and is currently handling the disposal, supervising the deployment of troops, and dealing with the aftermath. The battle in Chengdu is still fierce, and the enemy has suffered heavy losses. It will not be difficult to subdue them in the short term, according to a special dispatch on the 22nd.

(Chongqing) Street fighting broke out again in Chengdu on the 16th. Deng Xihou and Tian Songyao's troops fought against Liu Wenhui's army. Liu was defeated and led his guard brigade out of the province, retreating to Jiading. Tian and Deng's troops sent teams to occupy Xinjin and Shuangliu, cutting off Liu Wenhui's retreat to Kang. Liu Xiang transferred from Luzhou to Zijing to supervise the battle. The vanguard of the Chongqing army has reached Weiyuan and Rongxian. Zhang Qingping, Yang Shangzhou, Tian Boshi, and Gao Yucong, the division commander and brigade commanders who were ordered by Liu Wenhui to defend Luzhou, totaling more than 7,000 people, were surrounded and disarmed by Liu Xiang's army. Deng Xihou's chief of staff, Diao Wenjun, was killed by Liu Wenhui's troops. Deng was furious and ordered Huang Yin and Ma Dezhai's divisions, as well as Yang Xiuchun and Chen Li's brigades, to join the allied forces in attacking Liu, according to a special dispatch on the 22nd.

(Chongqing) Tian Songyao and Deng Xihou telegraphed Liu Xiang, reporting on the situation of the street fighting in the provincial capital and requesting instructions on the strategy, according to a special dispatch on the 22nd.

(Chongqing) Yang Sen and Li Jiayu personally supervised the allied forces in attacking the 24th Army. Yang himself has advanced to Zizhou, according to a special dispatch on the 22nd.

(Chongqing) Liu Xiang appointed Hou Zhidan, the Guizhou army division commander, as the commander of the Sichuan-Guizhou border defense. Hou led his troops to attack Liu Wenhui's army from the flank and has occupied counties such as Xuyong, Gusong, Jiang'an, and Naxi. Liu's situation is increasingly precarious, according to a special dispatch on the 22nd.

(Nanjing) At today's Executive Yuan meeting, Gu Mengyu and others proposed a plan to govern Sichuan. Executive Yuan Resolution: Zhu Jiahuai Reports on the Handling of China Merchants Steam Navigation Company; the Shandong Provincial Government Approves Liu Zhennian's Resignation

(Nanjing) The Executive Yuan held its 77th meeting on the 22nd, attended by Huang Shaoxiong, Luo Wengan, Gu Mengyu, Zhu Jiahuai, Shi Qingyang, Chen Shaokuan, Chen Gongbo, Liu Ruiheng, Chen Shuren, and Song Ziwen. Gan Naikang, Zou Lin, Shi Ying, Chen Yi, Duan Xipeng, Zeng Zhongming, Chu Minyi, and Peng Xuepei were present. Song Ziwen presided. (A) Zhu Jiahuai, the Minister of Communications, reported on the progress of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company secretly signing a 30 million tael loan contract with the foreign China General Edison Company, and that Li Guojie had been sent to the court for investigation and prosecution. An order was issued to the former supervisor, Chen Fumu, to come to Beijing immediately for questioning. (B) Matters for discussion: (1) Minister of Foreign Affairs Luo's submission regarding the resignation of Qian Tai, Director of the International Department, and the transfer of Zhu Hexiang to the post, with Lin Chunxian filling the remaining Councilor vacancy and Cao Bangzheng succeeding to the vacated Secretary position, was approved. (2) The resignation of Liu Zhennian, a member of the Shandong Provincial Government, was approved. (3) Resolutions: (1) Shuang Qing, member of the Guizhou Provincial Government and concurrently Director of the Department of Construction, was dismissed. Liu Minjie, a member of the Provincial Government, will concurrently serve as the Director of the Department of Construction. You Guocai will be a member of the Provincial Government. (4) The Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission Chairman Shi's submission regarding the draft organizational law of the Mongolian Banner Propaganda Envoys Office, the general budget for the 21st year, the list of salaries for employees, and the revised organization law, etc., which were reviewed and organized, please review and approve, was passed, according to a special dispatch on the 22nd.

(Nanjing) The Minister of Communications Zhu Jiahuai reported to the Executive Yuan on the 22nd on the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company case, as follows: This is to report on the matter. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company and the foreign China General Edison Company secretly signed a 30 million tael loan contract on September 5th and 6th of this year by former Supervisor Chen Fumu and former General Manager Li Guojie, and it was not reported to the Ministry of Communications. On November 11th, the four docks were suddenly transferred to the China General Edison Company for takeover. In the meantime, the Ministry of Communications issued strict orders on November 8th and 10th to investigate. The former General Manager Li Guojie then sent someone on the 12th to submit the contract, and secretly reported the contents on the 13th, requesting leniency. It was said that 300,000 taels of silver were obtained by secretly negotiating with the China General Edison Company by issuing a receipt from the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, and the checks from HSBC and Citibank were handed over to Chen Fumu, etc. He also publicly admitted to the Shanghai Municipal Government that there was nothing different. The then-President of the Yuan ordered Shanghai Mayor Wu to order the Public Security Bureau to place Li Guojie under surveillance first, pending investigation. Subsequently, an order from the Yuan was received to thoroughly investigate and report. We immediately ordered the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company to thoroughly investigate and report, and sent Li Guojie to the court for investigation and prosecution, and sent a telegram to the former supervisor, Chen Fumu, to come to Beijing immediately for questioning. According to the first and second telegrams, it was still said that he was waiting for the boat to return to Shanghai, but there was no definite date. After sending a telegram ordering him to come to Beijing immediately, two long telegrams suddenly came, strongly arguing and sophistry, with many evasions. His intention was to incite shareholders to confuse the public and create political problems in order to cover up his crimes. I believe that the case is significant, involves criminal statutes, and should await the court to handle it according to law. All the circumstances of handling the case are summarized in this report and respectfully submitted for your review. Minister of Communications Zhu Jiahuai, according to a telegram from the Central News Agency on the 22nd.

(Nanjing) The organizational regulations of the Mongolian Banner Propaganda Envoys Office were passed by the Executive Yuan meeting on the 22nd. Recent Central Tax Revenues

(Nanjing) Since the rebels seized the Northeast Customs, central government revenues have decreased by approximately two million [currency unit] per month. However, since implementing the policy of collecting taxes elsewhere, with careful management, national tax revenues have increased by about one million compared to the previous month. This month, the increase may exceed 1.5 million. Reasons: (1) Since August 4th, when customs duties on seven types of luxury goods were increased, monthly tax revenues, according to the original plan, could increase by one million. (2) Although the Northeast customs duties, nominally ours since the September 18th Incident last year, had in reality long been plundered completely, after the government formulated countermeasures and implemented the collection of Northeast customs duties elsewhere, tax revenues have seen some improvement. Next month is a peak month for customs duties and should see a further increase. (22nd Special Dispatch)

Henan Disaster Refugees Cause Trouble at Changxindian Station, Minor Conflict with Railway Police, Destroying Station Doors and Windows, Etc.

(Beiping) At 3:30 PM today, approximately 500 disaster refugees from Henan arrived at Changxindian on a train. At 4:30 PM, they were scheduled to transfer to a train to Pukou, but because there were no cars waiting at the station, the refugees wanted to get off the train. The railway police stopped them, but over 300 people forcibly disembarked, seized the railway police commander's baton, and used bricks and stones to destroy the glass doors and windows of the station. The railway police and the Public Security Bureau tried their best to persuade them, and the stationmaster and the Public Security Bureau negotiated with the refugees' representatives, ordering them to go to Zhengzhou and then transfer to Pukou. After the representatives agreed, at 6:10 PM, all the refugees boarded the train to Zhengzhou, and the disturbance was quelled. (22nd Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The Guangzhou Southwest National Foreign Affairs Association telegraphed about the dispute over Portugal occupying Hengqin Island. Another diplomat said that although the boundary line between Great and Small Hengqin Islands was not clearly demarcated in the 1887 Sino-Portuguese Treaty, it can be recognized as Chinese territory without a doubt. In the late Qing Dynasty, the Boundary Demarcation Minister, who was senior and humble, also did not demarcate the line. Some people suspect that the Macau side intends to invade and occupy the islands, but according to Portugal's explanation, there is absolutely no intention to invade and occupy. We also believe that the occupation is inaccurate, as Macau is adjacent to our territory, and a policy of peace and friendship should be adopted to ensure peaceful coexistence. The best solution now is for the Portuguese government to work with Tang Shaoyi to first demarcate a temporary boundary on the spot, clarifying the boundary of Hengqin and the territorial waters to avoid further misunderstandings. In the future, the central government should appoint a special boundary demarcation commissioner to formally demarcate the boundary with the Portuguese government's representative, which would be in line with the procedure. It is not known whether the Macau government can proceed accordingly. (22nd Special Dispatch)

Chen Gongbo Talks About the Steel Plant Site Not Yet Determined

(Nanjing) Chen Gongbo told people that the two previously assumed sites for the steel plant, Ma'anshan and Xiejiadian in Pukou, each have advantages and disadvantages, and the German businessmen also have their own opinions. In terms of terrain, Ma'anshan seems to be superior to Xiejiadian, but in terms of transportation, the opposite is true. The daily output of the steel plant is estimated to be more than 500 tons. Only 15 tons per day are needed for national defense. The remaining sales must seek convenient transportation to reduce costs in order to compete with foreign goods. The Ministry has now entrusted military experts to redraw the plant map and conduct precise research. Because the matter concerns national defense and is one of the central government's major construction projects, we must seriously consider the matter to avoid future regrets. Recently, I have sent my personal opinions to Chairman Chiang, seeking his views. It is expected that a decision can only be made after the Third Plenary Session. (22nd Special Dispatch)

British Parliament Reopens

▲ Reuters, London, 22nd: The British Parliament reopened today. The King and Queen attended the Parliament and delivered a speech, mentioning world problems, national finances, and the general economic situation. He especially hoped for the success of the World Economic Conference and good results from disarmament. He continued that regarding the proposals for the Indian constitution, the government will submit them to Parliament for resolution once the Round Table Conference is concluded. He also said that the government will soon put forward measures on unemployment insurance and other unemployment problems. This Parliament session was originally intended to focus on domestic affairs, but it will also address foreign affairs. At the beginning of the session, the US war debt issue is most important. A week ago, it was expected that the US would accept the UK's proposal to extend the payment deadline. However, according to news coming from the US every day, this hope may not be reliable. The British budget does not include funds for repaying the war debt. If the US must repay the debt, then it will be necessary to propose a supplementary budget and raise 28 million pounds sterling to cover it.

▲ Reuters, Washington, 21st: President Hoover is seeking to reduce next year's government budget by more than 500 million US dollars and is now focusing on consulting with Roosevelt on the war debt issue. Hitler's Hopes for Forming a Cabinet Remain Slim

▲ Reuters, Berlin, 21st: Hitler's hopes for forming a cabinet remain extremely slim. Hitler, his confidants, and former Deutsche Bank president Dr. Schacht spent from noon to evening today drafting a reply to President Hindenburg's conditions for appointing him as Chancellor. The conditions are as follows: (1) The members of the new cabinet must be approved by the President. (2) The President reserves the right to appoint General Schleicher as Minister of Defense and Neurath as Minister of Foreign Affairs. (3) The President requires that the new government's economic plan must be approved by him. (4) The new government should guarantee not to restore the "dualism" between Germany and Prussia. (5) The new cabinet must not attempt to reduce the powers granted to the President by Article 40 of the Constitution. Hitler is now trying his best to draft a reply that will satisfy the President, but political circles feel that Hitler's hopes of forming a cabinet under these conditions are very slim. Even if he fully accepts the President's conditions, he will not be able to obtain a majority of support in the parliament, as the Center Party has no strong desire to support him, and Hugenberg's National People's Party is very opposed to it. Hugenberg has not yet spoken to Hitler, but has refused to meet with Goering, the parliament chairman of the Nazi Party. If Hitler fails, President Hindenburg will likely ask the leader of the Center Party, Kaas, to try to obtain a majority in the parliament, but if the Nazi Party opposes it, Kaas will also fail. At this point, the President will only have one way out: to organize a presidential cabinet with a neutral leader, while retaining most of the members of the current government.

▲ Havas, 21st: Landes, France: Within the city of Landes, at the place where the order for the merger of Navarre with France was signed, the event is now 400 years ago. The whole city celebrated today. Prime Minister Herriot arrived late due to an accident on the railway, but the celebration ceremony proceeded as scheduled. The crowd flocked to the station to welcome the Prime Minister. The arrival of the train was met with thunderous cheers. Herriot went straight to the City Hall, where the Mayor gave a simple speech, stating that 400 years ago, the Princess of Navarre married the King of France, and Navarre was incorporated into France without any war. Herriot replied, saying that he would continue to strive to complete what Briand had not finished, in order to avoid the recurrence of war.

Looking at the future trend, all the most successful businesses will follow the principle of beneficial sharing. Special Feature

The Future of Withdrawing from the League of Nations and the South Seas Mandate (Continued)

(Professor Hikomatsu Kamikawa, Tokyo Imperial University, Japan)

▲ The League of Nations has the right to interpret the views adopted by the League of Nations in the past, and the most appropriate interpretation of the League of Nations Covenant should be the following theory, that is, the mandate has dual powers. The decision of the mandatory power and its changes belong to the main Allied and Associated Powers, but the administration of the mandated territory should be carried out in the name of the League of Nations and must be subject to the supervision of the League of Nations. In other words, the mandated territory is under the joint rule of the main Allied and Associated Powers and the League of Nations. This view was adopted by the Council of the League of Nations on August 5, 1920, in the Imans Report, which is the authorized interpretation adopted by the international community in the past, and there should be no errors.

▲ What attitude will the League of Nations take? The above international law considerations have been completed, and now it is time to observe the international political aspects. The theories about the granting and deprivation of the mandate power are as diverse as mentioned in the previous article. However, when Japan clashed head-on with the League of Nations due to the Manchurian Incident, resulting in its withdrawal from the League of Nations, what kind of theory would the League of Nations adopt? (?) This can only be determined by comprehensively observing the actual situation in international politics, the aversion of the League of Nations countries to Japan, and other various situations. It must not be rashly prejudged. However, I believe that the theory most easily adopted by the League of Nations should be the last one that the League of Nations adopted as an authoritative interpretation and has been adopted. If the League of Nations adopts this theory, what will be the status of Japan, the mandatory power, at that time? (?) It is not difficult to predict. Because according to this theory, all mandated territories should be under the joint control of the main Allied and Associated Powers and the League of Nations. If our country consistently opposes it, the League of Nations will not be able to deprive us of the mandate over the South Seas Islands. Needless to say.

▲ Because Japan is no longer a member of the League of Nations, a situation will arise where it acts as a mandated power by the League of Nations. Regarding this point, in the implementation of the mandate, we must be prepared to encounter various difficulties. According to Article 22, Paragraphs 7 and 9 of the League of Nations Covenant, the mandatory power should submit an annual report on the mandated territory to the League of Nations, which will be reviewed by the Permanent Mandates Commission. As a non-League of Nations country, it will inevitably encounter many difficulties if it wants to attend the Permanent Mandates Commission and the Council to express its opinions. This is another point that we should pay attention to.

▲ What about the worst-case scenario? However, the situation in international politics changes with the times, and the worst-case scenario must also be foreseen. Since the League of Nations regards Japan as an enemy country, it must adopt the aforementioned active theory in legal interpretation, that is, it must deprive Japan of the mandate it has obtained. If the situation reaches this point, what will be the fate of the mandated territory of the South Seas Islands? If the League of Nations decides to deprive Japan of its mandate, to which country will it be granted? I believe that there are two countries with the possibility of being granted: first, Germany; second, the United States.

When the first League of Nations General Assembly was held in 1920, Germany sent a memorandum to the General Assembly, stating that when deciding on the distribution of the old German mandated territories, Germany also had the right to be considered. If these territories are completely merged into the main Allied and Associated Powers under the name of mandate, it is suspected of violating Article 22 of the Covenant. By 1926, Germany joined the League of Nations and obtained the status of a permanent member of the Council. Germany further put forward a strong argument, saying that Germany is a culturally advanced country and has the most appropriate qualifications for assuming the responsibilities of mandate, such as resource experience. Germany is the old master of the mandated territory and is now a permanent member of the League of Nations Council. Of course, it has the right to participate in the mandate and share a piece of the pie. Moreover, among the League of Nations countries, in order to make Germany forget the suffering of defeat and join the League of Nations with peace of mind, there are also those who advocate that it must be given a mandate. In summary, based on past situations, once the League of Nations deprives Japan of its mandate, it may turn around and grant it to Germany, which is not a baseless statement. However, the mandated territory was originally ceded by Germany to the main Allied and Associated Powers. Therefore, when Japan is deprived of this right, it will still be granted to the United States, one of the main Allied and Associated Powers. It cannot be said that no one will make this claim. Judging from the international political situation in the past, this possibility seems to be slightly smaller than that of Germany. However, if we take a broader view of the relationship between Japan and the United States in the Pacific, it cannot be concluded that the United States has no hope of obtaining the mandate over the South Seas Islands.

If the League of Nations deprives our country of the mandate over the South Seas Islands and transfers it to Germany or the United States, this is the worst-case scenario. At this time, can our country obey the decision of the League of Nations? I know that it is impossible. If our country disregards this decision of the League of Nations and continues to rule the South Seas Islands, what will be the result? At this time, the League of Nations will inevitably resort to the navy to drive Japanese forces out of the South Seas Islands.

However, is the League of Nations or the newly mandated Germany or the United States willing to bet on a naval battle to fight for the control of the South Seas Islands? I dare say that this is impossible. In the end, it will only be recorded in the minutes of the League of Nations meeting that the South Seas Islands are a mandated territory of Germany or the United States, but in reality, they will still be occupied by us and remain under our rule. At this time, the League of Nations will inevitably regard Japan as an illegal occupying country and regard it as a public enemy of the League of Nations and criticize it. The future will be unimaginable. This is another thing that must be prepared for. (End)

The Shanghai Evening Post Vigorously Refutes Japan's Memorandum

Japan is Forcing an Old Style as the Latest Fashion

The Nine-Power Treaty Does Not Limit China to Time

Cannot Govern Others Without Their Permission

Lincoln's Famous Saying Must Be Implemented in Manchuria and the World

Japan's memorandum is full of sophistry and absurdity. Various newspapers have already commented and refuted it, and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs is also drafting a rebuttal. However, words from oneself may be regarded as subjective opinions. On the 20th, the Shanghai Evening Post published an article criticizing Japan for dressing up in 19th-century attire to show people, and claiming it to be the most fashionable new fashion. It also determined that Japan will eventually have to change its mind. The arguments are stern and just. The following is a translation of the original text:

The Foreign Affairs Agency translated the Shanghai Evening Post's commentary, saying that Japan's memorandum to the investigation team does not seem to have much new factual information. Even if there is, it is minimal. On the contrary, there is a large pile of repeated arguments. It is particularly evident that Japan cannot understand the new enlightenment of the modern thinking path of international events. Someone has repeatedly made remarks saying that Japan is an unfortunate country, permanently lagging behind and unable to catch up. Japan's extravagance is produced when the empire under the old meaning is becoming increasingly obsolete. Japan's efforts to defend its imperialist actions as reasonable are often based on precedents that have been invalidated by treaties and new international attitudes. Accordingly, Japan continues to work hard on things that have been done many years ago, and expresses anger at the criticism and genuine hostility caused by its actions based on modern concepts. Japan always wears a skirt with a padded bustle, a hat that is high in the front and low in the back, and displays a woman's new dress from 1856 to prove that what she is wearing is the latest outfit. There are several points in Japan's criticism that make people wonder. Did the person preparing Japan's reply actually carefully read the report? For example, there is a statement in it that the report's unfairness to Japan is discussed in a fragmented manner, and it cannot recognize a fundamental tenet, and make it smooth and integrated, that is, "there is a certain intention to eliminate Japan's rights in Manchuria." Speaking of the facts, the report thoroughly acknowledges the matter mentioned, but it is expressed in another sentence, "Implementing its, China's) national policy of restricting Japan's constant interests in Manchuria." This is the central point of disagreement between Lytton and Japan on Manchuria. The investigation team sees that "the national policy goals of China and Japan conflict with each other," and sees that they are those who enjoy "extraordinary interests" rather than those who enjoy "rights." And Japan's reply is based on the lofty basis that Japan is divinely endowed to reverse the chaos and restore order in an ownerless territory, nominally owned by a neighboring country that is completely unworthy of being called a "nation."

Looking at all the fundamental differences above, there will inevitably be three or four repetitions and top-heavy conflicts on every important point. The assumptions that the Japanese have from the beginning, that is, that the investigation team simply does not know what they are talking about, should be stopped and considered, and enter a more solid basis, that is, recognize that the investigation team does know it, but they are speaking from a completely different point of view from Japan. This point can be resolved immediately. Japan's criticism has returned to the Washington Conference, and it may not even be necessary to hold the same views as the investigation team. Japan now seems to be adopting a view of China that is very different from that of other signatory countries.

Japan claims to feel that all events have made the assumptions of 1922 deceived, and even conveyed the meaning that China's rapid progress should be a prerequisite for the treaty to continue to be effective. In fact, everyone can check the treaty to see that there is no such meaning in the text. The treaty orders the signatory countries to "respect China's sovereignty, independence, and territorial and administrative integrity," and requires the countries to "give China the fullest and least difficult opportunity to develop and maintain an effective and stable government." There is no time limit on the progress of China's development. The progress of China's national development, if there are ups and downs, is like what individuals have. In the eyes of an unbiased bystander, it seems to be quite natural. And Japan is now using the fact that things in Manchuria do not meet its criteria to create reasons to prove that its entire process in Manchuria is reasonable.

As mentioned earlier, there are countless points of top-heavy conflict between this reply and the Lytton Report. Japan not only continues to insist that the emergence of "Manchukuo" is a natural and independent event, but also further declares, "Japan believes that the future of Manchukuo is bright and promising." Try to compare this with Lytton's view, Lytton said, "The independence movement was unheard of in Manchuria before September 1931, only because the Japanese army was in the field of action was a clear thing." Also, the Chinese banker and merchant quoted Lytton as saying, "We do not want to become Koreans."

It is not necessary to elaborate on these dead ends, just remember how accidental they are and how directly they hinder the fundamental concepts of the Japanese officials and the investigation team. Lincoln said many years ago, "I am sure that without the permission of the other party, no one can govern others." This view will take the world a lot of time to see its value. Japan is proof that there are still people who do not believe it. But this is a truth, and the civilized view will eventually be implemented in Manchuria, and it will be implemented everywhere in the world. Those who recognize this fact will be spared from changing their minds later, or will have to change their minds themselves.

Hankou dispatch. Commander-in-Chief Chiang, in order to understand the situation at the front lines due to the remnants of bandits Xu and He fleeing to Shaanxi and Henan, took his own Sikorsky plane from Hankou on the 17th to inspect northern Hubei.
